  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_63cd7eea-56b5-4fc9-b545-10b894ae2754'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11441666934949067114">This complete and unabridged collection contains all 23 of Beatrix Potter's Tales in one deluxe volume with all their original illustrations.   <span id="freeText11441666934949067114" style="display:none">This complete and unabridged collection contains all 23 of Beatrix Potter's Tales in one deluxe volume with all their original illustrations. The stories are arranged in the order in which they were first published so they may be read in their proper sequence. A special section at the end of this volume contains four additional works by Beatrix Potter that were not published during her lifetime. Beautifully reissued with a newly designed slipcase and jacket--a truly stunning gift.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2878835115" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2878835115?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780723247609" href="/book/show/19332.The_Complete_Tales_of_Beatrix_Potter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=middlegrade">middlegrade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2878835115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2475072168718087885"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563504858i/27850659._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote>Beatrix Potter has written so many quintessential children's stories that even now, at 26 years old, I am overwhelmed with nostaglia and delight every time I pick this book up. <blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563504858i/27850657._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote>Unfortunately, I could not say the feeling was shared with my reading partner. <br/><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563504858i/27850658._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote> Seriously, Squamish (my dog) was such a brat as I tried to read this one. <blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563548018i/27854498._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote> He's lucky that he's so cute!<br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Tale of Peter Rabbit</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Your Father had an accident there, he was put in a pie by Mrs. McGregor</i>
</blockquote>Whewww ... Beatrix Potter c</span>
  <span id="freeText2475072168718087885" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563504858i/27850659._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>Beatrix Potter has written so many quintessential children's stories that even now, at 26 years old, I am overwhelmed with nostaglia and delight every time I pick this book up. <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563504858i/27850657._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>Unfortunately, I could not say the feeling was shared with my reading partner. <br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563504858i/27850658._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote> Seriously, Squamish (my dog) was such a brat as I tried to read this one. <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563548018i/27854498._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote> He's lucky that he's so cute!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Peter Rabbit</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Your Father had an accident there, he was put in a pie by Mrs. McGregor</i>
</blockquote>Whewww ... Beatrix Potter certainly didn't pull any punches. In this classic tale, Peter Rabbit (the naughty child) steals int Mr. McGregor's garden and filches all sorts of vegetables. Personally, if my husband was put into a pie, I would move out of their neighborhood...but it was a different time.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Squirrel Nutkin</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>This is a tale about a tail - a tail that belonged to a little red squirrel, and his name was Nutkin.</i>
</blockquote> The red squirrels visit an old, wise owl and Nutkin decides to act out and torment the poor owl. He's going to learn one very valuable lesson.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tailor of Gloucester</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>But although he sewed fine silk for his neighbours, he himself was very, very poor...</i>
</blockquote>An old tailor is about to lose everything...but the mice family may have a thing or two to do about it.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Benjamin Bunny</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>...little Benjamin Bunny slid down into the road, and set off - with a hop, skip and a jump...</i>
</blockquote>Benjamin Bunny discovers the trouble his cousin (Peter Rabbit) got into. So the two of them devise a sneaky plan...<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Two Bad Mice</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Tom Thumb and Hunca Munca went upstairs and peeped into the dining-room. Then they squeaked with joy!</i>
</blockquote>The nearby mice decide to check out the dollhouse. They cause quite a bit of mischief but decide to make things right in their own way.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Mrs. Tiggy-Winkle</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>She was a good little girl - only she was always losing her pocket-handkerchiefs!</i>
</blockquote>One lost handkerchief leads young Lucie on a whirlwind adventure and finds a pocket-handkin...which is the same?? <br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of The Pie and The Patty-Pan</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Once upon a time there was a Pussy-cat called Ribby, who invited a little dog called Duchess, to tea.</i>
</blockquote>Not many people would see the two of them as fast friends - but they are...however their diets may be an issue. Soon Duchess will have a scare of a lifetime.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Mr. Jeremy Fisher</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>...he lived in a little damp house amongst the buttercups at the edge of a pond.</i>
</blockquote> Mr. Jeremy Fisher is a saucy fella with an empty belly. There's a problem that arises when the food could hunt you!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Story of A Fierce Bad Rabbit</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>The bad Rabbit would like some carrot.<br>He Doesn't say "Please."<br>He takes it!</i>
</blockquote>For those who think that Peter Rabbit was too sweet - here is truly a bad bunny!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Story of Miss Moppet</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>This is the Mouse peeping out behind the cupboard, and making fun of Miss Moppet. He is not afraid of a kitten.</i>
</blockquote> A mischievous mouse and a curious kitten have a battle of wits - who will win?<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Tom Kitten</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Now keep your frocks clean, children! You must walk on your hind legs."</i>
</blockquote>Tom Kitten is quite possibly the sassiest kitten. When his mother's friends come to tea...well...let's just say he has a few plans of his own.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Jemima Puddle-Duck</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>She tried to hide her eggs; bit they were always found and carried off.</i>
</blockquote> Jemima Puddle-Duck wants only to raise her eggs away from the meddling influence of the humans. A "kind" fox helps her out - only she needs to learn how to be a bit judicious with her trust.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Samuel Whiskers or The Roly-Poly Pudding</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Oh, dear me, Cousin Ribby - now Moppet and Mittens are gone!</i>
</blockquote> Troublesome kittens, mischief being managed, and a couple of mean rats making trouble - what else could possibly go wrong!?<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of The Flopsy Bunnies</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>They had a large family, and they were very improvident and cheerful.</i>
</blockquote> Eating food, going on adventures and teasing Mr. McGregor - this family has it all.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Ginger and Pickles</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>They did accounts. They added up sums and sums, and sums.</i>
</blockquote> Ginger and Pickles run a convenience store - only running a store ends up being far more difficult than they imaged.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Mrs. Tittlemouse</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Mrs. Tittlemouse was a most terribly tidy particular little mouse, always sweeping and dusting the soft sandy floors.</i>
</blockquote> A little fussy mouse must deal with a greedy, messy frog.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Timmy Tiptoes</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>While Timmy was confined to bed, it 'ticed him him to eat quantities...</i>
</blockquote>A fat squirrel and a thin chipmunk have quite a fun adventure.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Mr. Tod</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Nobody could call Mr. Tod "nice."</i>
</blockquote>A family of young rabbits go missing and all signs point to Mr. Tod. Will they be saved in time? Or will Mr. Tod get his way?<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Pigling Bland</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>He glanced wistfully along the road towards the hills, and then set off walking obediently the other way.</i>
</blockquote>Eight piglets means many mouths to feed. Their poor mother is at her wits end when Pigling Bland decides to go on an adventure.<br><b>
  <u>Appley Dapply's Nursery Rhymes</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Appley Dapply has little sharp eyes,<br>And Appley Dapply is so fond of pies.</i>
</blockquote>A series of fun nursery rhymes with all sorts of cool and fun critters!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Johnny Town-Mouse</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Timmy Willie, who had lived all his life in a garden, was almost frightened to death.</i>
</blockquote>Based on Aesop's fable about the town and country mouse, Beatrix still manages to inject new life in this familiar tale. <br><br><b>
  <u>Cecily Parsley's Nursery Rhymes</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Goosey, Goosey, Gander,<br>Whither will you wander?<br>Upstairs and downstairs,<br>And in my lady's chamber!</i>
</blockquote>Several tried-and-true nursery rhymes are re-imagined a la Beatrix Potter. Absolutely delightful!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Tale of Little Pig Robinson</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Well, good day, little pig."</i>
</blockquote>Loosely based on seventeen-year-old Beatrix Potter's vacation on the seaside, this lovely little story follows Pig Robinson as he goes on quite the adventure!<br><br><b>
  <u>Three Little Mice</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Three little mice sat down to spin.</i>
</blockquote>An extremely short story, among Potter's earliest works. Her distinct art style is showcased splendidly. <br><br><b>
  <u>The Sly Old Cat</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>This is a sly old cat, who gave a tea party to a rat.</i>
</blockquote> Just goes to show, no matter the era, cats and rats do NOT mix!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Fox and the Stork</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>All he said was, "Tit for tat!"</i>
</blockquote>A selfish fox invites a gracious stork over for tea, and the stork decides to repay the favor. Mischief abound!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Rabbits' Christmas Party</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Dinner is served<br>The dancing begins</i>
</blockquote>A sweet but sparse tale all about rabbits and how they celebrate Christmas.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>While the audiobook was rather enjoyable, it really didn't have the same pizzazz as the physical book. The illustrations brought such a beautiful dimension to the text and the book truly isn't the same without them.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2475072168718087885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_454550564" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454550564" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454550564?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454550564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14987465842403826475">Don't let this innocent looking book fool you! It's all death and despair right from the get-go when a mother bunny relates with such nonchalant callousness the death of their father to four impressionable young rabbits. One suspects she wasn't all that sad to see the old man go. Perhaps he was beating her. <br/><br/>Love the fantastic illustrations! Sure they border on Kinkadian quaintness and might be too cute for their own good, but without them most of these stories quite frankly never would've been r</span>
  <span id="freeText14987465842403826475" style="display:none">Don't let this innocent looking book fool you! It's all death and despair right from the get-go when a mother bunny relates with such nonchalant callousness the death of their father to four impressionable young rabbits. One suspects she wasn't all that sad to see the old man go. Perhaps he was beating her. <br /><br />Love the fantastic illustrations! Sure they border on Kinkadian quaintness and might be too cute for their own good, but without them most of these stories quite frankly never would've been read. Beatrix Potter had a quirky writing style that was adequate most of the time, unexpectedly fun some of the time, and completely useless a time or two. If it weren't for the pictures, at least once or twice the reading would've ground to a "what huh?" halt.<br /><br />If there's an over-arching theme, aside from "FUZZY BUNNIES! SQUEEEEE!!!!!", it would be that of "Thievery in the world of the common man (or mouse)". Many of Potter's stories revolve around thieving, from petty pilfering to wholesale theft on a grand scale such as in "The Tale of the Tailor of Gloucester". The focal story of the collection, and the story everyone thinks of first, "The Tale of Peter Rabbit" is about a young thief eluding a vindictive farmer, who <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[upon failing to capture the little thief <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> creates an effigy using Peter's clothes in which "to frighten the blackbirds," a thinly veiled nod to the farmer's apparent racist attitude towards minorities. In each story the thief occasionally gets their comeuppance, other times they get away with it, and sometimes they are heralded like a Robin Hood for their acts. It's difficult to decipher Potter's stance, but it is clear the crime weighed heavily upon her mind. <br /><br />NOTE: I decided to write this serious (well, semi-serious) review after realizing my original review lacked much depth and insight. <br /><br /><br />ORIGINAL REVIEW:<br /><br />I love these stories sooooo much!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14987465842403826475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

They love the pictures, and the stories are fun and easy to follow for all ages. I've always loved THE TALE OF TWO BAD MICE best, but my son tells me that THE TALE OF THE FLOPSY BUNNIES is best, because they're so lazy and sleepy they almost get eaten.<br/><br/>2017: I don't think any of the illustrations could be better than the expression on Tom Kitten's face when </span>
  <span id="freeText13910002011056497602" style="display:none">The classic stories really do stand the test of time. I've read these aloud to my children over and over. Even my 7 year old boy loves them. They love the pictures, and the stories are fun and easy to follow for all ages. I've always loved THE TALE OF TWO BAD MICE best, but my son tells me that THE TALE OF THE FLOPSY BUNNIES is best, because they're so lazy and sleepy they almost get eaten.<br /><br />2017: I don't think any of the illustrations could be better than the expression on Tom Kitten's face when he puts on his clothes and they're too tight.</span>

<div id="review_2787994654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2787994654" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7897151-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461450073p2/7897151.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2787994654?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/7897151-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780723236184" href="/book/show/756711.The_Complete_Tales_of_Beatrix_Potter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897151-amanda?shelf=children-young-adult">children-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897151-amanda?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7897151-amanda?shelf=short-stories-essays">short-stories-essays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2787994654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17083632436339150585">This was so enjoyable! I did not grow up loving these as a child, but I think that worked to these tales’ advantage for me as an adult. I so appreciated the craft of these stories having read a Beatrix Potter biography alongside it. I really liked the writing style, stories’ messages, depictions of animal behavior and illustrations, both watercolor and pen-and-ink. I will continue to treasure these stories as I read them in the future.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2787994654">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_56051998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56051998" />
    <a title="Wayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1466146-wayne"><img alt="Wayne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56051998?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne" href="/user/show/1466146-wayne">Wayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780723236184" href="/book/show/756711.The_Complete_Tales_of_Beatrix_Potter">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone - Accountants perhaps not!!!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wayne by: </span>
      Beatrix's illustrations.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=art-and-artists">art-and-artists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=movie-seen-as-well">movie-seen-as-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=animals-as-stars">animals-as-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=plays">plays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=music">music</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=english-tales">english-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56051998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6861021763014502173">PRELUDE;<br/>A few weeks ago went to see the film of the Royal Ballet dancing several Tales of Beatrix Potter. The ballet choreographed by Frederick; with music, really delightful, by John Lanchbery, was first made into a film some years ago.This recent production was filmed in the actual theatre.<br/>There were only two of us in the movie theatre.I was sitting right at the back and was sorely tempted to get up and dance to my heart's content across the large open area behind the last row of seats. I didn</span>
  <span id="freeText6861021763014502173" style="display:none">PRELUDE;<br />A few weeks ago went to see the film of the Royal Ballet dancing several Tales of Beatrix Potter. The ballet choreographed by Frederick; with music, really delightful, by John Lanchbery, was first made into a film some years ago.This recent production was filmed in the actual theatre.<br />There were only two of us in the movie theatre.I was sitting right at the back and was sorely tempted to get up and dance to my heart's content across the large open area behind the last row of seats. I didn't... but I did cavort round the house when I got home and played the music.<br />I came to Beatrix Potter late, about age 31.(It's never TOO late!!) Took a break from my job in Athens to join my Mum and Step-father in a motoring holiday around the U.K. Was reading BP's biography by Margaret Lane - an excellent one. And so of course when we hit the Lake District we ended up at her wonderful house left exactly as she had left it. Mum photographed me standing in the doorway where BP had her photo taken.(I knew because the photo was in the book!!)<br />Later Mum was to run around the moors on the edge of Haworth crying out "Heathcliff!!Heathcliff!!!"in a much darker literary clime. After which we got caught in a Yorkshire storm and staggered into our hotel dying of laughter, while my step-father gave us fierce disapproving looks which made us laugh all the more.(He WAS an Accountant, and I'm sure had NEVER read a Beatrix Potter!!)<br />So now I am going to read first the several Tales that were recreated for the ballet. And then follow up with ALL the rest. The Music was...perfect, capturing their Essence...mice and ducks and foxes etc. ALL had had their Characters and Movements interpreted with the Ideal Notes, hidden away and NOW teased out into Life !!<br />Ah, blisssssss!!! <br /><br />MUCH LATER:<br />Now aged almost 62, short of a couple of weeks, I have read All the Tales in Chronological Order. And discovered that Beatrix has a Dark Side!!! (Scarey!!!)...not really, since she was a Realist, bit the bullet, had tasted<br /> disappointment in career prospects because she was a woman; a self-taught artist, as a girl she had drawn her pet animals ; as a young woman she had copied at the Natural History Museum animals and fossils AND 300 studies of fungi, the latter still regarded as perfect copies, but rejected then as not worthy of the Museum. <br />So she employed HERSELF - turned her skills to writing and illustrating Children's Books !! Six publishers rejected her first book. But finally F.Warne and Co. said "YES!" <br />The VERY FIRST story, The Tale of Peter Rabbit", Mrs Rabbit tells her children where they may and may not go, warning them off Mr.McGregor's garden :"...your Father had an accident there; he was put in a pie by Mrs McGregor."(Ouch!! There goes Junior's slumberful night!) But Beatrix never wrote down to children and her openess won her fans , not failure. Her marriage to the younger Warne brother, Norman, a kindred spirit, was NEVER to take place. He died of pernicious anaemia. It was now she bought herself a farm in the Lake District. The books , ALL illustrated by Beatrix, continued to flow and there was...and still is... a Constant Audience. <br />Often Beatrix's Own Inspirations for her animal characters didn't live to tell their Tale.<br />Mr Jeremy Fisher - dissected. Peter Rabbit - death by chloroform, followed by dissection and drawn for illustrative purposes. Jemima Puddleduck - ditto. And Squirrel Nutkin shot - at Beatty's request for drawing. And Guess Who performed the dissections. (Not a question!)<br /><br />Is it surprising then, given the blood on Beatty's hands, that every Tale has at least one sentence that lets Junior know all is NOT well with the World. Life itself is under threat. Even if its just Ginger, (the cat who shared ownership of the popular village shop with Pickles the terrier, popular because it gave generous credit), who had to ask Pickles to serve their mouse customers because they made his mouth water. ("I cannot bear to see them going out at the door carrying their little parcels," he confessed.) Pickles had to make a similar confession about rats, but being a Realist added:"..but it would never do to eat our own customers; they would leave us and go to Tabitha Twitchet's."(The cat whose shop did NOT give credit.)Being much more of a realist, which one would expect of a cat, Ginger replied gloomily:<br />"On the contrary,they would go nowhere."<br />Ginger"s and Pickle's business finally collapses because of their Customer's Greed<br />(ALL characters from the Tales I am shocked to tell you!!!).Allowed to buy on Credit,they NEVER paid a penny, so poor Ginger and Pickles were forced to eat their own goods...but never laid claw or tooth on their clientele, to THEIR credit !!! (No pun intended, I assure you!)Pickles became a gamekeeper and Ginger went to live on the warren and became stout and comfortable. Would it surprise you to learn that a warren is a place where rabbits abound? Although Miss Potter tells us:"I do not know what occupation he pursues", her drawing shows Ginger laying nasty traps with big metal teeth - on the warren!!!(Miss Potter's illustrations often convey information she does NOT provide in the text!!) AND Miss Tabitha Twitchett put up all her prices and refused to give credit!!!!!<br /><br />After this Tale of 1909 Miss Potter's Tales just get nastier and nastier. They are thrilling and delightful!! I'm sure All those Edwardian era Mums and Dads had no idea what subversiveness and violence was being smuggled into Junior's nursery under innocent covers. By 1912 Miss Potter had declared that she was tired of writing:<br />"goody goody books about nice people." <br />No wonder World War One broke out only a couple of years later. <br />And yet the History Books never mention Miss Potter as a possible Cause.<br />Nor does Feminism. <br /> <br />EPILOGUE:<br />Miss Potter knew a lot.<br />Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder???<br />Tom Kitten,victim of the rat, Anna Maria, who tied him up; and her husband, Mr.Samuel Whiskers, who helped her encase him in dough to be cooked and eaten.Poor Tom is rescued just in time. But ever afterwards "he has always been afraid of a rat; he never durst face anything that is bigger than - a mouse!"<br />And I doubt any sensitive reader will either.<br />Except the Insensitive who will no doubt join the Army.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6861021763014502173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788711310656" href="/book/show/21444579-de-samlede-eventyr-om-peter-kanin-og-hans-venner">review of another edition</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer998763356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10716975232842252694">I did not read these gorgeous tales when I was a child. I have no nostalgia for Peter Rabbit and his friends. But oh, how I wish I had! How I wish I had read about the wonderful rabbit in his lovely blue jacket with shiny golden buttons and his tiny pair of shoes. How I wish I had lost myself in Beatrix Potter's wonderful, pastel-coloured water-paintings and gasped of the wickedness and cunning of Tommy Brock, and sighed with delight with each happy ending, each last word wrapping up the story i</span>
  <span id="freeText10716975232842252694" style="display:none">I did not read these gorgeous tales when I was a child. I have no nostalgia for Peter Rabbit and his friends. But oh, how I wish I had! How I wish I had read about the wonderful rabbit in his lovely blue jacket with shiny golden buttons and his tiny pair of shoes. How I wish I had lost myself in Beatrix Potter's wonderful, pastel-coloured water-paintings and gasped of the wickedness and cunning of Tommy Brock, and sighed with delight with each happy ending, each last word wrapping up the story in a delicate ribbon.<br /><br />But even if I didn't read them as a child and even if I don't possess that cherished sense of nostalgia towards Beatrix Potter's universe of foxes, birds, squirrels and rabbits, I still found these tales to be an absolute delight, adorably simple and perfectly fitting for any child (or any child hiding within an adult). <br /><br />I can easily understand why these tales are so beloved and so dear to so many people. I can't understand why I haven't read them sooner. </span>

<div id="review_1713201432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713201432" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713201432?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780723247609" href="/book/show/19332.The_Complete_Tales_of_Beatrix_Potter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3498889-cheryl?shelf=xx-dnf-skim-reference">xx-dnf-skim-reference</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713201432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16605474610154362362">Ok, no, I didn't read the whole book, not even all the ones I didn't know before. After all, they're at Project Gutenberg, so I can read them on my tablet at any time. But I picked this up at the library to have an idea of just how prolific Potter (second cousin's great-aunt of Harry?) was. And I have to admit, the variety of what she created is more than I realized, and the quantity less. <br/><br/>I'm finding that I'm enjoying the ones that are not so cutesy bunny more than those that are. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375712.The_Tale_of_Mr__Tod' title='The Tale of Mr. Tod by Beatrix Potter' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Tale of M</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16605474610154362362" style="display:none">Ok, no, I didn't read the whole book, not even all the ones I didn't know before. After all, they're at Project Gutenberg, so I can read them on my tablet at any time. But I picked this up at the library to have an idea of just how prolific Potter (second cousin's great-aunt of Harry?) was. And I have to admit, the variety of what she created is more than I realized, and the quantity less. <br /><br />I'm finding that I'm enjoying the ones that are not so cutesy bunny more than those that are. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375712.The_Tale_of_Mr__Tod" title="The Tale of Mr. Tod by Beatrix Potter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tale of Mr. Tod</a> is killer. I never knew that Mr. Tod is a nickname for a fox, and Tommy Brock is a badger. And when a mother rabbit finds her children missing, we read that she "wrung her ears." <br /><br />Did you know also that Potter bought country lands to preserve it, and "When she died in 1943 she left over 4,000 acres and fifteen farms to the nation." </span>
  <a data-text-id="16605474610154362362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15044599778271736454">Ever since I saw Miss Potter, starring Renee Zellweger and Ewan McGregor, I have wanted to read Beatrix Potter's stories. Thankfully, my parents surprised me with a beautiful edition of her Complete Tales. Well, I guzzled it in a mere two days.   <span id="freeText15044599778271736454" style="display:none">Ever since I saw Miss Potter, starring Renee Zellweger and Ewan McGregor, I have wanted to read Beatrix Potter's stories. Thankfully, my parents surprised me with a beautiful edition of her Complete Tales. Well, I guzzled it in a mere two days. Yep, this one's a darling collection with gorgeous paintings and sketches by Miss Potter herself. I loved every moment of it and recommend it to anyone who still has a vivid imagination. You'll need one to see hedgehogs, pigs, and rabbits (among other critter friends) as "a dear person" (or people, as the case may be), as Miss Potter once described Mrs. Tiggy-winkle, her pet hedgehog. I couldn't be more delighted with this charming collection of stories, artwork, and brief histories of each tale and Beatrix Potter's life at the time she wrote them.<br /><br />Fans of Winnie the Pooh and Mary Poppins will love this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15044599778271736454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_387483941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/387483941" />
    <a title="Emma Long" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10953591-emma-long"><img alt="Emma Long" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342294606p2/10953591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/387483941?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Long" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Long" href="/user/show/10953591-emma-long">Emma Long</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer387483941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4085329583614887854">Beatrix Potter's Complete Tales holds a very dear place in my heart. This collection has never lost its popularity. Beatrix Potter's first story in 1902, "The Tale of Peter Rabbit" was published in a small edition by Frederick Warne, within a year it was an instant best seller. To this day the appeal of the tales is just as strong.<br/><br/>The animals seem to almost take on human personalities. In fact, these magical stories are often connected with real people, places or animals. Stories that involve an</span>
  <span id="freeText4085329583614887854" style="display:none">Beatrix Potter's Complete Tales holds a very dear place in my heart. This collection has never lost its popularity. Beatrix Potter's first story in 1902, "The Tale of Peter Rabbit" was published in a small edition by Frederick Warne, within a year it was an instant best seller. To this day the appeal of the tales is just as strong.<br /><br />The animals seem to almost take on human personalities. In fact, these magical stories are often connected with real people, places or animals. Stories that involve animals as the main characters in books always seem to fascinate young children and Peter Rabbit has always been up there with the best. <br /><br />The Tale of Mr Jeremy Fisher can provide the perfect introduction into mini-beasts such as beetles, grasshoppers and worms in KS1 science lessons. The life cycle of a frog can also be explored. Beatrix Potter can also be used in conjunction with History lessons on the Victorians. By studying Beatrix Potter's childhood, children can compare/contrast it with their own world. This can also lead way to discussions as to why Potter wrote simple stories about animals rather than people. Children can then go on to write their own animal themed story. With regards to Art lessons, children can draw a variety of animals and plants, they can then work with watercolour, just as Beatrix Potter did with her own illustrations.<br /><br />These tales are most certainly tailored to a younger audience, most certainly EYFS, yet these tales can and still are enjoyed by older audiences, including myself.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4085329583614887854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2412131403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16904061893068206989"><i>In all honesty, this probably deserves a 3.5 stars but, due to sentimentality and nostalgia, I'm just giving it a 4.</i><br/><br/>Beatrix Potter's stories have been a part of my life for a long time now - I regularly visit the Lakes (a place where Potter lived and bought these stories to life, as well as it thriving off Peter Rabbit merch), these stories were read to me in my childhood, and I've had two pets named after characters (an old rabbit called, you guessed it, Peter and my current dog Tiggi). I was e</span>
  <span id="freeText16904061893068206989" style="display:none"><i>In all honesty, this probably deserves a 3.5 stars but, due to sentimentality and nostalgia, I'm just giving it a 4.</i><br /><br />Beatrix Potter's stories have been a part of my life for a long time now - I regularly visit the Lakes (a place where Potter lived and bought these stories to life, as well as it thriving off Peter Rabbit merch), these stories were read to me in my childhood, and I've had two pets named after characters (an old rabbit called, you guessed it, Peter and my current dog Tiggi). I was eager to visit these stories. <br /><br />They don't mean as much to me as they used to do. I'm not a fan of children's literature (you only have to see my shelves to know that) - I tend to get really annoyed at the simple and basic things. I hate the patronising tone of voice, and the simplified language - all reasonable things. I didn't really find this was the case with Potter's work, instead I was just bored with the longer stories (I even stopped reading one of them because it was so uninteresting). I liked the nursery rhymes, and the shorter stories like Peter Rabbit, and Tom Kitten. I didn't like the ones to do with the Pigs, etc. <br /><br />Other than this one disadvantage, these stories were really pleasant to read. I loved being able to revisit certain stories - the ones that have stuck with me for a long time. I will never get bored of re-reading the Peter Rabbit story. They just aren't as fun to read now that I'm older, and that's totally okay. I'm surprised, to be honest, with the rating I've given it now - normally children's literature doesn't even get 3 stars!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16904061893068206989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer17882243554090996689">The Kindle edition included audio files which I didn't listen to, although I might try them at some future time.<br/><br/>When one thinks of Beatrix Potter, Peter Rabbit immediately springs (or hops) to mind, but there is so much more. Other stories feature rabbits, mice, cats, dogs, frogs, ducks, pigs, squirrels and other animals. Human beings usually appear only incidentally, and play a major role in only a few stories. The level of the narration varies: some stories seem geared to the very young, and s</span>
  <span id="freeText17882243554090996689" style="display:none">The Kindle edition included audio files which I didn't listen to, although I might try them at some future time.<br /><br />When one thinks of Beatrix Potter, Peter Rabbit immediately springs (or hops) to mind, but there is so much more. Other stories feature rabbits, mice, cats, dogs, frogs, ducks, pigs, squirrels and other animals. Human beings usually appear only incidentally, and play a major role in only a few stories. The level of the narration varies: some stories seem geared to the very young, and some to more mature audiences. They often feature animals getting into trouble through their own carelessness, which is a plot element often found in fairy tales. Problems are solved sometimes through ingenuity, sometimes through sheer luck. <br /><br />This edition contains Potter's illustrations, some in black and white, many in colour. I'm glad to say that none of the little animals moved mischievously when no one else was looking.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9459529314690653915">The first book I can remember reading was The Tale of Peter Rabbit, so Beatrix Potter is very near and dear to my heart. This collection of her tales is simply wonderful. Between her stunning artwork and her entertaining stories, there is something here for everyone. I </span>
  <span id="freeText9459529314690653915" style="display:none">The first book I can remember reading was The Tale of Peter Rabbit, so Beatrix Potter is very near and dear to my heart. This collection of her tales is simply wonderful. Between her stunning artwork and her entertaining stories, there is something here for everyone. These would definitely be fun stories to read out loud to children. <br /><br />In regards to this edition, I really enjoyed how before each tale, there was some background information on the story and what inspired Ms. Potter to write them. I never realized before reading this that so many of her tales have interconnected characters and details, which was neat. It was fun to see favorite characters popping up again. </span>

        <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manuel Alfonseca" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca">Manuel Alfonseca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3183240136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8397965501586775932">ENGLISH: In the biopic "Miss Potter," about the author's life, which has very little historical inaccuracies, it's mentioned at the end that Miss Potter's books are the most sold children books of all time. I assume they made these calculations for the English-speaking literary world, but even so, by 2006, when the film was released, Miss Potter's books had already been surpassed by the saga of Harry Potter (a curious coincidence in surnames), which has sold over 450 million copies in all the wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8397965501586775932" style="display:none">ENGLISH: In the biopic "Miss Potter," about the author's life, which has very little historical inaccuracies, it's mentioned at the end that Miss Potter's books are the most sold children books of all time. I assume they made these calculations for the English-speaking literary world, but even so, by 2006, when the film was released, Miss Potter's books had already been surpassed by the saga of Harry Potter (a curious coincidence in surnames), which has sold over 450 million copies in all the world. Although perhaps Harry Potter books are not considered to be written for children. Anyway, "Le Petit Prince" by St.Exupéry has sold about 140 million copies, and I suspect Miss Potter's books (even together) can't equal that figure.<br /><br />In this my second reading of the complete tales, those I have liked most are "The tale of the pie and the patty-pan," "The tale of Samuel Whiskers" (or "The roly-poly pudding") and "The tale of Mr. Tod." Although it's addressed to very small children, I also like "The story of Miss Moppet," but that's perhaps due to the fact that I like cats and books about cats, and that Miss Potter's drawings in this tale are quite touching.<br /><br />The tales I liked less were "The Flopsy bunnies," "Ginger &amp; Pickles" and "Timmy Tiptoes." As to "Little Pig Robinson," it was too slow for my taste.<br /><br />ESPAÑOL: En la película biográfica "Miss Potter", sobre la vida de la autora, que tiene pocas imprecisiones históricas, se menciona al final que los libros de Miss Potter son los libros infantiles más vendidos de todos los tiempos. Supongo que sus cálculos se referían sólo al mundo literario de habla inglesa, pero aun así, en 2006, cuando se estrenó la película, los libros de Miss Potter ya habían sido superados por la saga de Harry Potter (curiosa la coincidencia de apellidos), que ha vendido más de 450 millones de ejemplares en todo el mundo. Aunque quizá es que no consideran que los libros de Harry Potter sean para niños. De todos modos, dado que "Le Petit Prince" de St.Exupéry ha vendido alrededor de 140 millones de ejemplares, no creo que los libros de Miss Potter (ni siquiera juntos) puedan igualar esa cifra.<br /><br />En esta mi segunda lectura de los cuentos completos, los que más me han gustado son "El cuento de la torta y el molde", "El cuento de Samuel Whiskers" (o "El pudín de roly-poly") y "El cuento de Mr. Tod". Aunque se dirige a niños muy pequeños, también me gusta mucho "La historia de Miss Moppet", pero quizá eso se deba al hecho de que me gustan los gatos y los libros sobre gatos, y que los dibujos de Miss Potter para este cuento son muy atractivos.<br /><br />Los cuentos que menos me gustaron fueron "Los conejitos de Flopsy", "Ginger y Pickles" y "Timmy Tiptoes". En cuanto a "Little Pig Robinson", es demasiado lento para mi gusto.</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780723247609" href="/book/show/19332.The_Complete_Tales_of_Beatrix_Potter">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954636657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14347597226901897107">I'm glad I got to revisit these stories as an adult reader. I, as many people, grew up with Beatrix Potter's stories - in particular The tale of Peter Rabbit although I've read a few others too as a child. Some of the stories were quite fun - I especially liked The tailor of Gloucester, The tale of two bad mice, and The tale of the pie and the patty-pan for the writing. Overall, the writing wasn't what drew me in - it's rather straight forward as its aimed at a young reader. But I love Beatrix P</span>
  <span id="freeText14347597226901897107" style="display:none">I'm glad I got to revisit these stories as an adult reader. I, as many people, grew up with Beatrix Potter's stories - in particular The tale of Peter Rabbit although I've read a few others too as a child. Some of the stories were quite fun - I especially liked The tailor of Gloucester, The tale of two bad mice, and The tale of the pie and the patty-pan for the writing. Overall, the writing wasn't what drew me in - it's rather straight forward as its aimed at a young reader. But I love Beatrix Potter for her art - her illustrations are so beautiful! It's interesting to see how her art style changes over the span of the stories; I prefer the more intricate style of the early years. One of the things I like about her animal characters is that they have a nice blend of actual animal characteristcs and human behavior - rather than being straight-up anthropomorphic. </span>

    <a title="Nicola Mansfield" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1682713-nicola-mansfield"><img alt="Nicola Mansfield" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510729582p2/1682713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola Mansfield" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola Mansfield" href="/user/show/1682713-nicola-mansfield">Nicola Mansfield</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780723244042" href="/book/show/1202778.The_Complete_Tales">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698007798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10366997363045225882">Review written in 2007: I've been reading this aloud to my 7yo for a month or so, reading one story every now and then. The stories are presented here in chronological order as published with 4 unpublished works at the end. The stories are wonderful, darling tales of anthropomorphic animals. Once she married in 1913 she didn't have as much time for her painting and writing and I think it shows as the stories in the first half of the book are much more enjoyable than the latter ones. The stories </span>
  <span id="freeText10366997363045225882" style="display:none">Review written in 2007: I've been reading this aloud to my 7yo for a month or so, reading one story every now and then. The stories are presented here in chronological order as published with 4 unpublished works at the end. The stories are wonderful, darling tales of anthropomorphic animals. Once she married in 1913 she didn't have as much time for her painting and writing and I think it shows as the stories in the first half of the book are much more enjoyable than the latter ones. The stories are somewhat didactic but not overly so. They are also much more violent than I would have remembered them to be. Naughty children are spanked frequently and Potter presents as a matter of fact that animals are often killed by hunters, farmers and other animals.<br /><br />The 7yo really enjoyed the stories, especially the ones in which Peter Rabbit or members of his family appeared. Also, while each story stands alone there are references to prior events and characters and this was fun to notice when reading them in order. This edition itself includes a brief biography of Beatrix Potter at the front and prior to each story is a short introductory paragraph detailing connections in the story with Potter's real life. All the original illustrations, including the original front covers illustrations, are included and this is a book that can be browsed through just for the gorgeous watercolours and sketches.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10366997363045225882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_935325633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/935325633" />
    <a title="Shawn Thrasher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2148308-shawn-thrasher"><img alt="Shawn Thrasher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549498919p2/2148308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/935325633?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawn Thrasher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawn Thrasher" href="/user/show/2148308-shawn-thrasher">Shawn Thrasher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780786152445" href="/book/show/9950073-the-complete-tales-of-beatrix-potter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer935325633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9810141973171855533">I listened to the magnificently read Blackstone audio version, and really, I can't recommend it enough. It's like having a British gran read you the stories before a crackling fire while English weather does what English weather does outside, with a cup of chamomile tea. <br/><br/>Tennyson wrote "Nature, red in tooth and claw" and while he wasn't writing about the brutal world of Beatrix Potter, he could have been. Peter Rabbit and friends may be late Victorian yeomen and gentry wearing blue coats and sel</span>
  <span id="freeText9810141973171855533" style="display:none">I listened to the magnificently read Blackstone audio version, and really, I can't recommend it enough. It's like having a British gran read you the stories before a crackling fire while English weather does what English weather does outside, with a cup of chamomile tea. <br /><br />Tennyson wrote "Nature, red in tooth and claw" and while he wasn't writing about the brutal world of Beatrix Potter, he could have been. Peter Rabbit and friends may be late Victorian yeomen and gentry wearing blue coats and selling peppermints in shops, but they also have no absolutely no compunction about eating, skinning and wearing one another. "Would you care for a piece of pie, Duchess?" Ribby asks. "It WAS Mrs. Tittlemouse." Some of them also, horror of horrors, smoke (albeit rabbit tobacco). <br /><br />Some of these stories go absolutely no where, fast ("The Tale of Pigling Bland", for example) and don't really work all that well as stories - but when they do work, they are brilliant little gems; it's no wonder they are still in print, and will continue to be in print, until Peter Rabbit is a folk character the same as his cousin Br'er Rabbit. So long live the stories of Beatrix Potter!<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9810141973171855533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_265932882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265932882" />
    <a title="Helen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4151280-helen"><img alt="Helen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288974458p2/4151280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265932882?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen" href="/user/show/4151280-helen">Helen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265932882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7962787129825349011">These are kids' books?!?!?! Seriously?!?!<br/>I have no problem with anthropomorphic personifications, talking rabbits etc, but surely if you're making the animals talk you should stay away from making them eat each other! It may be because I was 'reading' the complete series on audiobook, one after the other, but do we have to have one story telling the tale of the mice that 'live' in the dolls house when the kids aren't playing with it and then in the very next story have the dog eating mouse pie? </span>
  <span id="freeText7962787129825349011" style="display:none">These are kids' books?!?!?! Seriously?!?!<br />I have no problem with anthropomorphic personifications, talking rabbits etc, but surely if you're making the animals talk you should stay away from making them eat each other! It may be because I was 'reading' the complete series on audiobook, one after the other, but do we have to have one story telling the tale of the mice that 'live' in the dolls house when the kids aren't playing with it and then in the very next story have the dog eating mouse pie? Or the cat running the general store refuse to serve the mice because his mouth waters too much?!?! If we're personifying the creatures surely that's canibalism?<br />And yes, I'm aware these are classics and have been around for close to 100 years, this is only my take on it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7962787129825349011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_262025015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262025015" />
    <a title="Beth Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728103-beth-anne"><img alt="Beth Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564681652p2/4728103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262025015?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Anne" href="/user/show/4728103-beth-anne">Beth Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262025015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2801996106114070079">This was a read aloud book to Emma. I think I loved the stories as much as she did! I read most, if not all, of these when I was little, but I had forgotten much of the stories.<br/><br/>Children's stories certainly are not written like this anymore. I love that Beatrix Potter uses brilliant and colorful language. Her characters and descriptions were simple, endearing, and full of life. The illustrations are simple but there is something about them that captures your heart. She was a gifted lady to be sur</span>
  <span id="freeText2801996106114070079" style="display:none">This was a read aloud book to Emma. I think I loved the stories as much as she did! I read most, if not all, of these when I was little, but I had forgotten much of the stories.<br /><br />Children's stories certainly are not written like this anymore. I love that Beatrix Potter uses brilliant and colorful language. Her characters and descriptions were simple, endearing, and full of life. The illustrations are simple but there is something about them that captures your heart. She was a gifted lady to be sure.<br /></span>

<div id="review_51927845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51927845" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177816-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484852290p2/2177816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51927845?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/2177816-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177816-anne?shelf=children-s-books-and-literature">children-s-books-and-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177816-anne?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51927845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3780305044974363977">You might think that the big words and adult phrasing in these books would deter a child's interest... not so! Children love stories about animals, and even if they don't understand every word (or -sometimes - even the plot!), they enjoy the rhythm of the language, the pictures and the funny situations. Besides, reading books like this with more advanced vocabulary and sentence structure teaches them how to speak with more advanced vocabulary and more complex sentences.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122867299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122867299" />
    <a title="Joanne Valiukas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4119080-joanne-valiukas"><img alt="Joanne Valiukas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442510851p2/4119080.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122867299?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne Valiukas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne Valiukas" href="/user/show/4119080-joanne-valiukas">Joanne Valiukas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122867299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9515904477541825006">I adore these little stories which are always so delightfully engaging and fun. I used to make my husband read them to me when I couldn't sleep and my favourite was always The Pie and the Patty Pan. Just like Ribby or Mrs Ribston as she is known in the tale, my husband came home to a chicken pot pie that had just underneath the crust...yes, you guessed it...a patty pan. Me and our children roared with laughter at the delighted shock on his face. Ms Potter and I...we got him good.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X4Kbr3wAK2hfyiH9sAa209tqn1ItQHiL9HszYTghX0A/92phKkFr5teZ8E2XMb5LVYs+Dq9nuKMDia7yGyli2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ARrolSJjQJYrCvrE9VgtPbW7WSUu1bRzmM4Qhc7QBDRhbxlbdCIAGKNZK3TSbyWlO1r4eazydFtvPI0W7dg5rg==')})
  }

In Linda Lear\'s enchanting new biography, we get the life story of this incredible, funny, and independent woman. As one of the first female naturalists in the world, Potter brought the beauty and importance of nature back into the imagination at a time when plunder was more popular than preservation. Through her art she sought to encourage conservation and change the world. With never before seen illustrations and intimate detail, Lear goes beyond our perrenial fascination with Potter as a writer and illustrator of children\'s books, and delves deeply into the life of a       var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_2998'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2998.The_Secret_Garden?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Secret Garden<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/2041.Frances_Hodgson_Burnett?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Frances Hodgson Burnett<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.13 avg rating &mdash; 898,010 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1910\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer8415840008094954204\">\"One of the most delightful and enduring classics of children\'s literature, The Secret Garden by Victorian author Frances Hodgson Burnett has remained a firm favorite with children the world over ever since it made its first appearance. Initially pub<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8415840008094954204\" style=\"display:none\">&quot;One of the most delightful and enduring classics of children\'s literature, The Secret Garden by Victorian author Frances Hodgson Burnett has remained a firm favorite with children the world over ever since it made its first appearance. Initially published as a serial story in 1910 in The American Magazine, it was brought out in novel form in 1911.  The plot centers round Mary Lennox, a young English girl who returns to England from India, having suffered the immense trauma by losing both her parents in a cholera epidemic. However, her memories of her parents are not pleasant, as they were a selfish, neglectful and pleasure-seeking couple. Mary is given to the care of her uncle Archibald Craven, whom she has never met. She travels to his home, Misselthwaite Manor located in the gloomy Yorkshire, a vast change from the sunny and warm climate she was used to. When she arrives, she is a rude, stubborn and given to stormy temper tantrums. However, her nature undergoes a gradual transformation when she learns of the tragedies that have befallen her strict and disciplinarian uncle whom she earlier feared and despised. Once when he\'s away from home, Mary discovers a charming walled garden which is always kept locked. The mystery deepens when she hears sounds of sobbing from somewhere within her uncle\'s vast mansion. The kindly servants ignore her queries or pretend they haven\'t heard, spiking Mary\'s curiosity.  The Secret Garden appeals to both young and old alike. It has wonderful elements of mystery, spirituality, charming characters and an authentic rendering of childhood emotions and experiences. Commonsense, truth and kindness, compassion and a belief in the essential goodness of human beings lie at the heart of this unforgettable story. It is the best known of Frances Hodgson Burnett\'s works, though most of us have definitely heard of, if not read, her other novel Little Lord Fauntleroy.  The book has been adapted extensively on stage, film and television and translated into all the world\'s major languages. In 1991, a Japanese anime version was launched for television in Japan. It remains a popular and beloved story of a child\'s journey into maturity, and a must-read for every child, parent, teacher and anyone who would enjoy this fascinating glimpse of childhood. One of the most delightful and enduring classics of children\'s literature, The Secret Garden by Victorian author Frances Hodgson Burnett has remained a firm favorite with children the world over ever since it made its first appearance. Rebecca’s father had died three years before and the family farm had become heavily indebted. In order to ease the burden on her widowed mother, Rebecca is sent to live with her lonely aunts at their farm and there she spends the next seven years till she becomes an adult. Rebecca brings her youthful enthusiasm and imagination to their quiet life and often clashes with her stern Aunt Miranda. Yet, Rebecca finds love and acceptance with her Aunt Jane and she grows up to be a proper and intelligent young lady who never loses her sunny outlook and kind heart. “Rebecca of Sunnybrook Farm” is a classic coming of age story that has been adapted numerous times for the stage and screen and continues to charm audiences and readers alike with its interesting characters and positive message of       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11593.Beatrix_Potter">About Beatrix Potter</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11593.Beatrix_Potter"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1560035067p3/11593.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/11593.Beatrix_Potter">Beatrix Potter
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,607
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16691471054246081503">Helen Beatrix Potter was an English author, illustrator, mycologist, and conservationist who is best known for her children's books, which featured animal characters such as Peter Rabbit.<br/><br/>Born into a wealthy household, Potter was educated by governesses and grew up isolated from other children. She had numerous pets, and through holidays in Scotland and the Lake District, developed a love of landsc</span>
  <span id="freeText16691471054246081503" style="display:none">Helen Beatrix Potter was an English author, illustrator, mycologist, and conservationist who is best known for her children's books, which featured animal characters such as Peter Rabbit.<br /><br />Born into a wealthy household, Potter was educated by governesses and grew up isolated from other children. She had numerous pets, and through holidays in Scotland and the Lake District, developed a love of landscape, flora, and fauna, all of which she closely observed and painted. Because she was a woman, her parents discouraged intellectual development, but her study and paintings of fungi led her to be widely respected in the field of mycology.<br /><br />In her thirties, Potter published the highly successful children's book <i>The Tale of Peter Rabbit</i> and became secretly engaged to her publisher, Norman Warne, causing a breach with her parents, who disapproved of his social status. Warne died before the wedding.<br /><br />Potter eventually published 24 children's books, the most recent being <i>The Tale of Kitty-in-Boots</i> (2016), and having become financially independent of her parents, was able to buy a farm in the Lake District, which she extended with other purchases over time. <br /><br />In her forties, she married a local solicitor, William Heelis. She became a sheep breeder and farmer while continuing to write and illustrate children's books. Potter died in 1943 and left almost all of her property to The National Trust in order to preserve the beauty of the Lake District as she had known it, protecting it from developers.<br /><br />Potter's books continue to sell well throughout the world, in multiple languages. Her stories have been retold in various formats, including a ballet, films, and in animation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16691471054246081503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
